<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Violence_against_women" title="Template:Violence against women"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Violence_against_women&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>

<p><b>Sexual slavery</b> is <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> for the purpose of sexual <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/exploitation" title="wikt:exploitation">exploitation</a>. Sexual slavery may involve single-owner sexual slavery; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ritual_slavery" title="Ritual slavery">ritual slavery</a>, sometimes, associated with certain religious practices, such as <a href="/wiki/Ritual_servitude" title="Ritual servitude">ritual servitude</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>; slavery for primarily non-sexual purposes but where non-consensual <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">sexual activity</a> is common; or <a href="/wiki/Forced_prostitution" title="Forced prostitution">forced prostitution</a>. <a href="/wiki/Concubinage" title="Concubinage">Concubinage</a> was a traditional form of sexual slavery in many cultures, in which women spent their lives in sexual servitude. In some cultures, concubines and their children had distinct rights and legitimate social position</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Declaration_and_Programme_of_Action" title="Vienna Declaration and Programme of Action">Vienna Declaration and Programme of Action</a> calls for an international effort to eradicate sexual slavery as an abuse of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>. The incidence of sexual slavery by country has been studied and tabulated by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, with the cooperation of various international agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute (1998)</a> (which defines the crimes over which the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> may have jurisdiction) encompasses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" title="Crime against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> (Article 7) which include "enslavement" (Article 7.1.c) and "sexual enslavement" (Article 7.1.g) "when committed as part of a widespread or systematic attack directed against any civilian population". It also defines sexual enslavement as a <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a> and a breach of the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> when committed during an international armed conflict (Article 8.b.xxii) and indirectly in an internal armed conflict under Article(8.c.ii), but the courts jurisdiction over war crimes is explicitly excluded from including crimes committed during "situations of internal disturbances and tensions, such as riots, isolated and sporadic acts of violence or other acts of a similar nature" (Article 8.d).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rome-Statute_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rome-Statute-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The text of the Rome Statute does not explicitly define sexual enslavement, but does define enslavement as "the exercise of any or all of the powers attaching to the right of ownership over a person and includes the exercise of such power in the course of trafficking in persons, in particular women and children" (Article 7.2.c).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rome-Statute_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rome-Statute-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the commentary on the Rome Statute,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_Klamberg" title="Mark Klamberg">Mark Klamberg</a> states:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iclklamberg.com_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-iclklamberg.com-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juridicas.unam.mx_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-juridicas.unam.mx-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Sexual slavery is particular form of enslavement which includes limitations on one's autonomy, freedom of movement and power to decide matters relating to one's sexual activity. Thus, the crime also includes <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">forced marriages</a>, domestic servitude or other forced labor that ultimately involves forced sexual activity. In contrast to the crime of rape, which is a completed offence, sexual slavery constitutes a continuing offence. ... Forms of sexual slavery can, for example, be practices such as the detention of women in "rape camps" or "comfort stations", forced temporary "marriages" to soldiers and other practices involving the treatment of women as chattel, and as such, violations of the peremptory norm prohibiting slavery.</p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Type">Type</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Type">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sex_trafficking">Sex trafficking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sex trafficking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking" title="Sex trafficking">Sex trafficking</a></div>
<p>Sex trafficking is a type of <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> involving the recruitment, transportation, transfer, harbour or receipt of people, by coercive or abusive means for the purpose of sexual exploitation. Sex trafficking is not the only form of human trafficking and estimates vary as to the percentage of human trafficking which is for the purpose of transporting someone into sexual slavery.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> cited a report by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_on_Drugs_and_Crime" title="United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime">UNODC</a> as listing the most common destinations for victims of human trafficking in 2007 as Thailand, Japan, Israel, Belgium, the Netherlands, Germany, Italy, Turkey and the US. The report lists Thailand, China, Nigeria, Albania, Bulgaria, Belarus, Moldova and Ukraine as major sources of trafficked persons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-UN-traffic_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-UN-traffic-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_sexual_exploitation_of_children">Commercial sexual exploitation of children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Commercial sexual exploitation of children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Commercial_sexual_exploitation_of_children" title="Commercial sexual exploitation of children">Commercial sexual exploitation of children</a></div>
<p>Commercial sexual exploitation of children (CSEC) includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prostitution_of_children" title="Prostitution of children">prostitution of children</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">child pornography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_sex_tourism" title="Child sex tourism">child sex tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trafficking_of_children" title="Trafficking of children">trafficking of children</a> for sexual purposes, or other forms of transactional sex with children. The Youth Advocate Program International (YAPI) describes CSEC as a form of <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violence" title="Violence">violence</a> against children and a contemporary form of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yapi.org_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-yapi.org-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clift_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-clift-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>A declaration of the World Congress Against the Commercial Sexual Exploitation of Children, held in Stockholm in 1996, defined CSEC as, "sexual abuse by the adult and remuneration in cash or in kind to the child or to a third person or persons. The child is treated as a sexual object and as a commercial object".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clift_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-clift-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_prostitution">Child prostitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Child prostitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prostitution_of_children" title="Prostitution of children">Prostitution of children</a></div>
<p>The prostitution of children is a form of <a href="/wiki/Commercial_sexual_exploitation_of_children" title="Commercial sexual exploitation of children">commercial sexual exploitation of children</a> in which a child performs the services of <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a>, usually for the financial benefit of an adult.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s federal police said in 2009 that they believed around 1.2 million children in India to be involved in prostitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-10">[10]</a></sup> A CBI statement said that studies and surveys sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Women_and_Child_Development" title="Ministry of Women and Child Development">Ministry of Women and Child Development</a> estimated about 40% of India's prostitutes to be children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thailand’s Health System Research Institute reported that children in prostitution make up 40% of prostitutes in Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unicri.it_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-unicri.it-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In some parts of the world, child prostitution is tolerated or ignored by the authorities. Reflecting an attitude which prevails in many developing countries, a judge from <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> said, on condition of anonymity: "If the victim [the child prostitute] is older than 12, if he or she refuses to file a complaint and if the parents clearly profit from their child's commerce, we tend to look the other way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_pornography">Child pornography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Child pornography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">Child pornography</a></div>
<p>Child pornography, sometimes referred to as 'child abuse images',<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wortley_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wortley-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanderson_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sanderson-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akdeniz11_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Akdeniz11-15">[15]</a></sup> refers to images or films depicting <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">sexually explicit</a> activities involving a child. As such, child pornography is often a visual record of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finkelhor1994_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-finkelhor1994-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hobbs_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-hobbs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-O-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheldon20_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheldon20-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klain_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Klain-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wortley17_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wortley17-21">[21]</a></sup> Abuse of the child occurs during the sexual acts which are photographed in the production of child pornography,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finkelhor1994_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-finkelhor1994-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hobbs_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-hobbs-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheldon20_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-sheldon20-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klain_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Klain-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wortley17_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wortley17-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheldon9_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-sheldon9-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO1999_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO1999-23">[23]</a></sup> and the effects of the abuse on the child (and continuing into maturity) are compounded by the wide distribution and lasting availability of the photographs of the abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wortley17_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wortley17-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sheldon9_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-sheldon9-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doj1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-doj1-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Child_sex_tourism">Child sex tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Child sex tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Child_sex_tourism" title="Child sex tourism">Child sex tourism</a></div>
<p>Child sex tourism is travel to a foreign country for the purpose of engaging in commercially facilitated child sexual abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deptstate_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-deptstate-25">[25]</a></sup> Child sex tourism results in both mental and physical consequences for the exploited children, that may include "disease (including HIV/AIDS), drug addiction, pregnancy, malnutrition, social ostracism, and possibly death", according to the State Department of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deptstate_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-deptstate-25">[25]</a></sup> Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, India, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> have been identified as leading hotspots of child sexual exploitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_prostitution">Forced prostitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Forced prostitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Forced_prostitution" title="Forced prostitution">Forced prostitution</a></div>
<p>Most, if not all, forms of forced prostitution may be viewed as a kind of sexual slavery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The terms "forced prostitution" and "enforced prostitution" appear in international and humanitarian conventions but have been insufficiently understood and inconsistently applied. "Forced prostitution" generally refers to conditions of control over a person who is coerced by another to engage in sexual activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reportof1998_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reportof1998-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The issue of consent in prostitution is hotly debated. Opinion in places such as Europe has been divided over the question of whether prostitution should be considered as a free choice or as inherently exploitative of women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The law in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> – where it is illegal to pay for sex, but not to sell sexual services – is based on the notion that all forms of prostitution are inherently exploitative, opposing the notion that prostitution can be voluntary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In contrast, prostitution is a recognized profession in countries such as the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and Germany.</p>
<p>In 1949 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> adopted the <a href="/wiki/Convention_for_the_Suppression_of_the_Traffic_in_Persons_and_of_the_Exploitation_of_the_Prostitution_of_Others" title="Convention for the Suppression of the Traffic in Persons and of the Exploitation of the Prostitution of Others">Convention for the Suppression of the Traffic in Persons and of the Exploitation of the Prostitution of Others</a> (the 1949 Convention). The 1949 Convention supersedes a number of earlier conventions that covered some aspects of forced prostitution. Signatories are charged with three obligations under the 1949 Convention: prohibition of trafficking, specific administrative and enforcement measures, and social measures aimed at trafficked persons. The 1949 Convention presents two shifts in perspective of the trafficking problem in that it views prostitutes as victims of the procurers, and in that it eschews the terms "white slave traffic" and "women," using for the first time race- and gender-neutral language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-entrepeneur_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-entrepeneur-31">[31]</a></sup> Article 1 of the 1949 Convention provides punishment for any person who "[p]rocures, entices or leads away, for purposes of prostitution, another person" or "[e]xploits the prostitution of another person, even with the consent of that person." To fall under the provisions of the 1949 Convention, the trafficking need not cross international lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-entrepeneur_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-entrepeneur-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_marriage">Forced marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Forced marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Forced_marriage" title="Forced marriage">Forced marriage</a></div>
<p>A forced marriage is a marriage where one or both participants are married, without their freely given consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Forced marriage is a form of sexual slavery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iclklamberg.com_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-iclklamberg.com-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juridicas.unam.mx_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-juridicas.unam.mx-6">[6]</a></sup> Causes for forced marriages include customs such as <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a>; poverty; the importance given to female premarital virginity; "<a href="/wiki/Family_honor" title="Family honor">family honor</a>"; the fact that marriage is considered in certain communities a social arrangement between the extended families of the bride and groom; limited education and economic options; perceived protection of cultural or religious traditions; assisting immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Forced marriage is most common in parts of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_against_humanity">Crime against humanity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Crime against humanity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute</a> Explanatory Memorandum, which defines the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>, recognizes rape, sexual slavery, forced prostitution, <a href="/wiki/Forced_pregnancy" title="Forced pregnancy">forced pregnancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">forced sterilization</a>, "or any other form of sexual violence of comparable gravity" as <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crime against humanity</a> if the action is part of a widespread or systematic practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horton_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Horton-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Sexual slavery was first recognized as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" title="Crime against humanity">crime against humanity</a> when the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> issued arrest warrants based on the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> and Violations of the Laws or Customs of War. Specifically, it was recognised that Muslim women in <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da" title="Foča">Foča</a> (southeastern <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>) were subjected to systematic and widespread gang rape, torture and sexual enslavement by Bosnian Serb soldiers, policemen, and members of paramilitary groups after the takeover of the city in April 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated17_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated17-41">[41]</a></sup> The indictment was of major legal significance and was the first time that sexual assaults were investigated for the purpose of prosecution under the rubric of torture and enslavement as a crime against humanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated17_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated17-41">[41]</a></sup> The indictment was confirmed by a 2001 verdict by the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> that rape and sexual enslavement are crimes against humanity. This ruling challenged the widespread acceptance of rape and sexual enslavement of women as intrinsic part of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmnestyInt2001feb22_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyInt2001feb22-42">[42]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</a> found three Bosnian Serb men guilty of rape of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosniac" title="Bosniac">Bosniac</a> (Bosnian Muslim) women and girls – some as young as 12 and 15 years of age – in <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da" title="Foča">Foča</a>, eastern Bosnia and Herzegovina. The charges were brought as <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_crimes" title="War crimes">war crimes</a>. Furthermore, two of the men were found guilty of the crime against humanity of sexual enslavement for holding women and girls captive in a number of de facto detention centers. Many of the women had subsequently disappeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmnestyInt2001feb22_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-AmnestyInt2001feb22-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In areas controlled by Islamic militants, non-Muslim women are enslaved in occupied territories. Many Islamists see the abolition of slavery as forced upon Muslims by the West and want to revive the practice of slavery.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavery_in_21st_century_Islamism" title="Slavery in 21st century Islamism">Slavery in 21st century Islamism</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bride_kidnapping_and_raptio">Bride kidnapping and raptio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Bride kidnapping and raptio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bride_kidnapping" title="Bride kidnapping">Bride kidnapping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raptio" title="Raptio">raptio</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="907" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg/220px-Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg/330px-Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg/440px-Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poussin_RapeSabineLouvre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_the_Sabine_Women" title="The Rape of the Sabine Women">The Rape of the Sabine Women</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Poussin" title="Nicolas Poussin">Nicolas Poussin</a>, Rome, 1637–38 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louvre_Museum" title="Louvre Museum">Louvre Museum</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bride kidnapping, also known as marriage by abduction or marriage by captive, is a form of forced <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> practised in some traditional cultures. Bride kidnapping has reportedly occurred in countries spanning <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">the Caucasus region</a>, parts of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and among the <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong</a> in southeast Asia, the <a href="/wiki/Tzeltal_people" title="Tzeltal people">Tzeltal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a> in Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Though the motivations behind bride kidnapping vary by region, the cultures with traditions of marriage by abduction are generally <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchal</a> with a strong <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">social stigma</a> against sex or pregnancy outside marriage and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegitimacy" title="Illegitimacy">illegitimate births</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stross_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-stross-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In most cases, however, the men who resort to capturing a wife are often of lower <a href="/wiki/Social_status" title="Social status">social status</a>, whether because of poverty, disease, poor character or criminality. In some cases, the couple collude together to elope under the guise of a bride kidnapping, presenting their parents with a fait accompli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stross_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-stross-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> These men are sometimes deterred from legitimately seeking a wife because of the payment the woman's family expects, the <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a> (not to be confused with a <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a>, paid <i>by</i> the woman's family).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stross_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-stross-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MongolsInHungary1285.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="825" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/MongolsInHungary1285.jpg/220px-MongolsInHungary1285.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/MongolsInHungary1285.jpg/330px-MongolsInHungary1285.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/MongolsInHungary1285.jpg/440px-MongolsInHungary1285.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MongolsInHungary1285.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Hungary" title="Mongol invasion of Hungary">Mongol invasion of Hungary</a>. The Mongols, with captured women, are on the left, the Hungarians, with one saved woman, on the right.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bride kidnapping is distinguished from <i>raptio</i> in that the former refers to the abduction of one woman by one man (and/or his friends and relatives), and is often a widespread and ongoing practice. The latter refers to the large-scale abduction of women by groups of men, most frequently in a time of war (see also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_rape" title="War rape">war rape</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Latin term raptio refers to abduction of women, either for marriage (by <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping" title="Kidnapping">kidnapping</a> or <a href="/wiki/Elopement" title="Elopement">elopement</a>) or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enslavement" title="Enslavement">enslavement</a> (particularly sexual slavery). In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">canon law</a>, raptio refers to the legal prohibition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrimony" title="Matrimony">matrimony</a> if the bride was abducted forcibly (Canon 1089 <a href="/wiki/Canon_law_(Catholic_Church)" title="Canon law (Catholic Church)">CIC</a>).</p>
<p>The practice of raptio is surmised to have existed since anthropological antiquity. In <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Europe" title="Neolithic Europe">Neolithic Europe</a>, excavation of a <a href="/wiki/Linear_Pottery_culture" title="Linear Pottery culture">Linear Pottery culture</a> site at <a href="/wiki/Asparn_an_der_Zaya" title="Asparn an der Zaya">Asparn-Schletz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, unearthed the remains of numerous slain victims. Among them, young adult females and children were clearly under-represented, suggesting that perhaps the attackers had killed the men but abducted the young females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_armed_conflict_and_war">During armed conflict and war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: During armed conflict and war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wartime_sexual_violence" title="Wartime sexual violence">Wartime sexual violence</a></div>
<p>Rape and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> have accompanied warfare in virtually every known historical era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levinson2004_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levinson2004-48">[48]</a></sup> Before the 19th century, military circles supported the notion that all persons, including unarmed women and children, were still the enemy, with the belligerent (nation or person engaged in conflict) having conquering rights over them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated11_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated11-49">[49]</a></sup> "To the victor goes the spoils" has been a war cry for centuries and women were included as part of the spoils of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated14_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated14-50">[50]</a></sup> Institutionalised sexual slavery and enforced prostitution have been documented in a number of wars, most notably the Second World War. ( See <a href="#During_the_Second_World_War">#During the Second World War</a> )</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_cases">Historical cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Historical cases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">Ancient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ancient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_and_Roman_Empire">Greek and Roman Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Greek and Roman Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sexuality_in_ancient_Rome" title="Sexuality in ancient Rome">Sexuality in ancient Rome</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_domination_of_Vietnam" title="Chinese domination of Vietnam">Chinese domination of Vietnam</a>, Vietnamese girls were sold as sex slaves to the Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The poet <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Zhen" title="Yuan Zhen">Yuan Chen</a> wrote a poem which contained the line "Slave girls of Viet (Yüeh), sleek of buttery flesh". A large trade developed where the native girls of Vietnam were enslaved and brought north to the Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Southern Yue girls were sexually eroticized in Chinese literature and in poems written by Chinese who were exiled to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 16th and 17th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> visitors and their <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Lascar" title="Lascar">lascar</a></i> (and sometimes African) crewmembers often engaged in <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Japan" title="Slavery in Japan">slavery in Japan</a>, where they bought or captured young <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese</a> women and girls, who were either used as sexual slaves on their ships or taken to <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonies</a> in Southeast Asia, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">the Americas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leupp-49_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leupp-49-59">[59]</a></sup> and India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leupp-52_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leupp-52-60">[60]</a></sup> For example, in <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese colony in India</a>, there was a community of Japanese slaves and traders during the late 16th and 17th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leupp-49_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leupp-49-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leupp-52_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leupp-52-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1662 <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Zeelandia" title="Siege of Fort Zeelandia">Siege of Fort Zeelandia</a> in which Chinese <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming</a> loyalist forces commanded by <a href="/wiki/Koxinga" title="Koxinga">Koxinga</a> besieged and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> and conquered Taiwan, the Chinese took Dutch women and children prisoner. The Dutch missionary <a href="/wiki/Antonius_Hambroek" title="Antonius Hambroek">Antonius Hambroek</a>, two of his daughters, and his wife were among the Dutch prisoners of war with Koxinga. Koxinga sent Hambroek to Fort Zeelandia demanding he persuade them to surrender or else Hambroek would be killed when he returned. Hambroek returned to the Fort, where two of his other daughters were. He urged the Fort not to surrender, and returned to Koxinga's camp. He was then executed by decapitation, and in addition to this, a rumor was spreading among the Chinese that the Dutch were encouraging the native Taiwan aboriginals to kill Chinese, so Koxinga ordered the mass execution of Dutch male prisoners in retaliation, in addition to a few women and children also being killed. The surviving Dutch women and children were then turned into slaves. Koxinga took Hambroek's teenage daughter as a concubine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and Dutch women were sold to Chinese soldiers to become their wives, the daily journal of the Dutch fort recorded that "the best were preserved for the use of the commanders, and then sold to the common soldiers. Happy was she that fell to the lot of an unmarried man, being thereby freed from vexations by the Chinese women, who are very jealous of their husbands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manthorpe77_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-manthorpe77-64">[64]</a></sup> In 1684 some of these Dutch wives were still captives of the Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Some Dutch physical looks like auburn and red hair among people in regions of south Taiwan are a consequence of this episode of Dutch women becoming concubines to the Chinese commanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manthorpe77_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-manthorpe77-64">[64]</a></sup> The Chinese took Dutch women as slave concubines and wives and they were never freed: in 1684 some were reported to be living, in Quemoy a Dutch merchant was contacted with an arrangement to release the prisoners which was proposed by a son of Koxinga's but it came to nothing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The Chinese officers used the Dutch women they received as concubines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manthorpe77_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-manthorpe77-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The Dutch women were used for sexual pleasure by Koxinga's commanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> This event of Dutch women being distributed to the Chinese soldiers and commanders was recorded in the daily journal of the fort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manthorpe77_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-manthorpe77-64">[64]</a></sup> A teenage daughter of the Dutch missionary Anthonius Hambroek became a concubine to Koxinga, she was described by the Dutch commander Caeuw as "a very sweet and pleasing maiden".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Dutch language accounts record this incident of Chinese taking Dutch women as concubines and the date of Hambroek's daughter<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 19th and early 20th centuries, there was a network of Chinese prostitutes trafficked to cities like <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and a separate network of Japanese prostitutes being <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Asia" title="Prostitution in Asia">trafficked across Asia</a>, in countries such as China, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, Singapore and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>, in what was then known as the ’Yellow Slave Traffic’. There was also a network of prostitutes from <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a> being <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_India" title="Prostitution in India">trafficked to India</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Ceylon" title="British Ceylon">Ceylon</a>, Singapore, China and Japan at around the same time, in what was then known as the ’White Slave Traffic’.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FischerTine2003_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FischerTine2003-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karayuki-san" title="Karayuki-san">Karayuki-san</a> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja" xml:lang="ja">唐行きさん</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>, literally "Ms. Gone-to-China" but actually meaning Ms. Gone Abroad")</span> were Japanese girls and women in the late 19th and early 20th centuries who were trafficked from poverty stricken agricultural prefectures in Japan to destinations in <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>), <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a> to serve as prostitutes and sexually serviced men from a variety of races, including Chinese, Europeans, native Southeast Asians, and others. In the 19th and early 20th centuries, there was a network of Japanese prostitutes being <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Asia" title="Prostitution in Asia">trafficked across Asia</a>, in countries such as China, Japan, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_India" title="British India">British India</a>, in what was then known as the ’Yellow Slave Traffic’.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FischerTine2003_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-FischerTine2003-76">[76]</a></sup> The main destinations of <i>karayuki-san</i> included <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (particularly Shanghai), <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Philippines" title="The Philippines">the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and the western USA (in particular San Francisco). They were often sent to Western colonies in Asia where there was a strong demand from Western military personnel and Chinese men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The experience of Japanese prostitutes in China was written about in a book by a Japanese woman, Tomoko Yamazaki.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Japanese girls were easily trafficked abroad since Korean and Chinese ports did not require Japanese citizens to use passports and the Japanese government realized that money earned by the karayuki-san helped the Japanese economy since it was being remmitted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and the Chinese boycott of Japanese products in 1919 led to reliance on revenue from the karayuki-san.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Since the Japanese viewed non-westerners as inferior, the karayuki-san Japanese women felt humiliated since they mainly sexually served Chinese men or native Southeast Asians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Borneo natives, Malaysians, Chinese, Japanese, French, American, British and men from every race utilized the Japanese prostitutes of Sandakan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> A Japanese woman named Osaki said that the men, Japanese, Chinese, whites, and natives, were dealt with alike by the prostitutes regardless of race, and that a Japanese prostitute's "most disgusting customers" were Japanese men, while they used "kind enough" to describe Chinese men, and the English and Americans were the second best clients, while the native men were the best and fastest to have sex with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> organised a governmental system of "<a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">comfort women</a>", which is a <a href="/wiki/Euphemism" title="Euphemism">euphemism</a> of military sex slaves for the estimated 200,000, mostly Korean, Chinese, and Filipino women who were forced into sexual slavery in <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Japanese military</a> "comfort stations" during World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english.chosun.com_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-english.chosun.com-97">[97]</a></sup> Japan collected, carried, and confined Asian ladies coercively and collusively to have sexual intercourse with Japan's soldiers during their invasions across <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> and Southeast Asia. Some Korean women claim that these cases should be judged by an international tribunal as child sex violence. The legal demand has been made because of the victims' anger at what they see as the inequity of the existing legal measures and the denial of Japan's involvement in child sex slavery and kidnapping. On the 28th of December 2015, Japan and South Korea agreed that Japan would pay 1 billion Yen into a fund for a Memorial Hall of comfort women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Despite this agreement, some Korean victims have complained that they were not consulted during the negotiation process. They demand that Japan and Korea did not seek both the legal recognition of their claim and the revision of Japanese history textbooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_slave_trade">Arab slave trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Arab slave trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">Slavery in the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<p>Slave trade, including trade of sex slaves,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> fluctuated in certain regions in the Middle East up until the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> These slaves came largely from <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> (mainly <i><a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a></i>), the Caucasus (mainly <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Central Asia (mainly <a href="/wiki/Sogdia" title="Sogdia">Sogdians</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Eastern Europe (mainly <i><a href="/wiki/Saqaliba" title="Saqaliba">Saqaliba</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_pirate" title="Barbary pirate">Barbary pirates</a> also captured 1.25 million slaves from <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> between the sixteenth and nineteenth centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-researchnews.osu.edu_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-researchnews.osu.edu-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis.2C_Robert_1999_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis.2C_Robert_1999-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>In contrast to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> where the male-female ratio was 2:1 or 3:1, the Arab slave trade usually had a higher female:male ratio instead, suggesting a general preference for female slaves. <a href="/wiki/Concubinage" title="Concubinage">Concubinage</a> and reproduction served as incentives for importing female slaves (often European), though many were also imported mainly for performing household tasks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ehud1998_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ehud1998-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="White_slavery">White slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: White slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geromeslavemarket.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1949" data-file-width="1452" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Geromeslavemarket.jpg/220px-Geromeslavemarket.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Geromeslavemarket.jpg/330px-Geromeslavemarket.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Geromeslavemarket.jpg/440px-Geromeslavemarket.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geromeslavemarket.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Slave Market</i> (c. 1884), painting by <a href="/wiki/Jean-L%C3%A9on_G%C3%A9r%C3%B4me" title="Jean-Léon Gérôme">Jean-Léon Gérôme</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In English-speaking countries in the 19th and early 20th centuries, the phrase "white slavery" was used to refer to sexual enslavement of white women. It was particularly associated with accounts of women enslaved in Middle Eastern <a href="/wiki/Harem" title="Harem">harems</a>, such as the so-called <a href="/wiki/Circassian_beauties" title="Circassian beauties">Circassian beauties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The phrase gradually came to be used as a euphemism for prostitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The phrase was especially common in the context of the exploitation of minors, with the implication that children and young women in such circumstances were not free to decide their own fates.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_White_Slave_statue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1090" data-file-width="926" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_White_Slave_statue.jpg/220px-The_White_Slave_statue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_White_Slave_statue.jpg/330px-The_White_Slave_statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_White_Slave_statue.jpg/440px-The_White_Slave_statue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_White_Slave_statue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue entitled <i>The White Slave</i> by <a href="/wiki/Abastenia_St._Leger_Eberle" title="Abastenia St. Leger Eberle">Abastenia St. Leger Eberle</a>, a controversial sculpture meant to depict modern western sexual enslavement.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a>, campaigning journalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Thomas_Stead" title="William Thomas Stead">William Thomas Stead</a>, editor of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pall_Mall_Gazette" title="Pall Mall Gazette">Pall Mall Gazette</a></i>, procured a 13-year-old girl for £5, an amount then equal to a labourer's monthly wage (<i>see</i> the <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Armstrong_case" title="Eliza Armstrong case">Eliza Armstrong case</a>). <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">Moral panic</a> over the "traffic in women" rose to a peak in England in the 1880s. At the time, "white slavery" was a natural target for defenders of public morality and crusading journalists. The ensuing outcry led to the passage of antislavery legislation in Parliament. Parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Law_Amendment_Act_1885" title="Criminal Law Amendment Act 1885">1885 Criminal Law Amendment Act</a>, raising the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a> from thirteen to sixteen in that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_perla_del_mercader.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1633" data-file-width="1040" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/La_perla_del_mercader.jpg/220px-La_perla_del_mercader.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/La_perla_del_mercader.jpg/330px-La_perla_del_mercader.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/La_perla_del_mercader.jpg/440px-La_perla_del_mercader.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_perla_del_mercader.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Merchant's Pearl</i> by <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Valenzuela_Puelma" title="Alfredo Valenzuela Puelma">Alfredo Valenzuela Puelma</a>,<br/>
(c. 1884)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A subsequent scare occurred in the United States in the early twentieth century, peaking in 1910, when <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._attorney" title="U.S. attorney">U.S. attorney</a> announced (without giving details) that an international crime ring was abducting young girls in Europe, importing them, and forcing them to work in Chicago <a href="/wiki/Brothel" title="Brothel">brothels</a>. These claims, and the <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">panic</a> they inflamed, led to the passage of the United States <a href="/wiki/Mann_Act" title="Mann Act">White-Slave Traffic Act</a> of 1910, generally known as the "Mann Act". It also banned the interstate transport of females for immoral purposes. Its primary intent was to address prostitution and immorality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Immigration inspectors at <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a> in New York City were held responsible for questioning and screening European prostitutes from the U.S. Immigration inspectors expressed frustration at the ineffectiveness of questioning in determining if a European woman was a prostitute, and claimed that many were "lying" and "framing skillful responses" to their questions. They were also accused of negligence should they accept a fictitious address from an immigrant or accept less-than-complete responses. Inspector Helen Bullis investigated several homes of assignment in the Tenderloin district of New York, and found brothels existed in the early 20th century in New York City. She compiled a list of houses of prostitutes, their proprietors, and their "inmates."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moloney2012_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moloney2012-114">[114]</a></sup> The New York inspection director wrote a report in 1907, defending against accusations of negligence, saying there was no sense to the public "panic," and he was doing everything he could to screen European immigrants for prostitution, especially unmarried ones. In a report by the Commissioner General of Immigration in 1914, the Commissioner said that many prostitutes would intentionally marry American men to secure citizenship. He said that for prostitutes, it was "no difficult task to secure a disreputable citizen who will marry a prostitute" from Europe.</p>
<p>Chinese immigrants in the U.S. were singled out as white slavers. As an example of this in American culture, the musical comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Thoroughly_Modern_Millie" title="Thoroughly Modern Millie">Thoroughly Modern Millie</a></i> features a Chinese-run prostitution ring, which is specifically referred to as "white slavery". The gangster movie <i><a href="/wiki/Prime_Cut" title="Prime Cut">Prime Cut</a></i> has mid-West white slaves sold like cattle.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_sexual_slavery_in_the_United_States" title="History of sexual slavery in the United States">History of sexual slavery in the United States</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking_in_the_United_States" title="Sex trafficking in the United States">Sex trafficking in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">Slavery in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Female_slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Female slavery in the United States">Female slavery in the United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forced_prostitution#USA" title="Forced prostitution">Forced prostitution § USA</a></div>
<p>From the beginning of African slavery in the North American colonies, white men took African enslaved women as concubines or occasional mistresses. As populations increased, slave women might be taken advantage of by white overseers, planter's younger sons before they married, and other white men associated with the slaveholders. Some were sold into brothels outright.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Pla%C3%A7age" title="Plaçage">Plaçage</a></i>, a formalized system of concubinage among slave women or <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a>, developed in Louisiana and particularly New Orleans by the 18th century. Young mixed-race women (considered highly desirable) would receive a dowry or property as part of an associated settlement negotiated by their mothers with white men. The fathers would often pay for education of their mixed-race children born of these unions, especially sons, who might be educated in France and enter the army. In recent years, at least three historians (<i>viz.</i> Kenneth Aslakson, Emily Clark, and Carol Schlueter) have challenged the <a href="/wiki/Historicity" title="Historicity">historicity</a> of Quadroon balls and have referred to the institution of Plaçage as "a myth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>But, Paul Heinegg's research showed that most mixed-race, <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free black</a> families in the censuses of 1790–1810 were descended from unions between free white women and African men, whether free, indentured servant or slave, that took place in colonial Virginia. It had half the slaves in the colonies at the time of the Revolution. In the early colonial years, the working class of indentured servants and slaves often worked and lived together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the 17th century, Virginia and other colonies passed laws determining the social status of children born in the colonies. Under English common law in England, children of two English subjects took the status of the father. But Africans were never considered English subjects. To settle the issue of the status of children born in the colony, Virginia passed a law in 1662 that ruled that children would take the status of their mother at birth, under the Roman legal principle known as <i><a href="/wiki/Partus_sequitur_ventrem" title="Partus sequitur ventrem">partus sequitur ventrem</a>.</i> Thus all children born to enslaved mothers were legally slaves, regardless of the paternity or ancestry of their fathers. They were bound for life and could be sold like any slave unless formally freed.</p>
<p>The term "white slaves" was sometimes used for those <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> or mulatto slaves who had a visibly high proportion of European ancestry. Among the most notable at the turn of the 19th century was <a href="/wiki/Sally_Hemings" title="Sally Hemings">Sally Hemings</a>, who was 3/4 white and believed by historians to be a half sister of <a href="/wiki/Martha_Jefferson" title="Martha Jefferson">Martha Wayles Skelton Jefferson</a> by their common father <a href="/wiki/John_Wayles" title="John Wayles">John Wayles</a>. Hemings is known for having four surviving children from her decades-long concubinage with President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>; they were 7/8 European by ancestry. Three of these mixed-race children passed easily into white society as adults. (Jefferson freed them all – two informally and two in his will.) Three of his Hemings grandsons served as white men in the Union Regular Army in the American Civil War; <a href="/wiki/John_Wayles_Jefferson" title="John Wayles Jefferson">John Wayles Jefferson</a> advanced to the rank of colonel.</p>
<p>Not all white fathers abandoned their slave children; some provided them with education or apprenticeships, or capital; some wealthy planters sent their mixed-race children to the North for education, and sometimes for freedom. Some men freed both their slave mistresses and their mixed-race children, especially in the 20 years after the American Revolution, but southern legislatures made such manumissions more difficult. Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_Chesnut" title="Mary Chesnut">Mary Chesnut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fanny_Kemble" title="Fanny Kemble">Fanny Kemble</a> wrote in the 19th century about the scandal of white men having their mistresses and natural <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">mixed-race</a> children as part of their extended households. Numerous mixed-race families were begun before the Civil War, and many originated in the Upper South.</p>
<p>After slaves were emancipated, many states passed <a href="/wiki/Anti-miscegenation_laws" title="Anti-miscegenation laws">anti-miscegenation laws</a>, which prohibited <a href="/wiki/Interracial_marriage" title="Interracial marriage">interracial marriage</a> between whites and non-whites. But this did not stop white men from taking sexual advantage of black women by using their social positions of power under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Crow" title="Jim Crow">Jim Crow</a> system and <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacy</a>, or in other parts of the country by ordinary power and wealth dynamics. For instance, in the 20th century futre politician <a href="/wiki/Strom_Thurmond" title="Strom Thurmond">Strom Thurmond</a> at age 21 had a sexual relationship with a 16-year-old maid in his parents' household and she became pregnant. He did provide support for their daughter. The girl was officially raised by her maternal aunt and uncle, not learning about her biological parents until she was in her late teens. She met Thurmond. She said nothing publicly about her status as his daughter until after Thurmond's death. With his family's agreement, her name has been added as one of his children on his memorial.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zora_Neale_Hurston" title="Zora Neale Hurston">Zora Neale Hurston</a> wrote about contemporary sexual practices in her <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropological</a> studies in the 1930s of the turpentine camps of North <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. She noted that white men with power often forced black women into sexual relationships.</p>
<p>Although she never named the practice as "paramour rights," author C. Arthur Ellis ascribed this term to the fictionalized Hurston in his book, <i>Zora Hurston and the Strange Case of Ruby McCollum.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The same character asserted that the death knell of paramour rights was sounded by the trial of <a href="/wiki/Ruby_McCollum" title="Ruby McCollum">Ruby McCollum</a>, a black woman who murdered Dr. C. Leroy Adams, in <a href="/wiki/Live_Oak,_Florida" title="Live Oak, Florida">Live Oak, Florida</a>, in 1952. She said he had forced her into sex and bearing his child. Journalist Hurston covered McCollum's trial in 1952 for the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Courier" title="Pittsburgh Courier">Pittsburgh Courier</a></i>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a> in the late 1840s, Chinese merchants transported thousands of young Chinese girls, including babies, from China to the United States. They sold the girls into sexual slavery within the red light district of San Francisco. Girls could be bought for $40 (about $1104 in 2013 dollars) in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, and sold for $400 (about $11,040 in 2013 dollars) in the United States. Many of these girls were forced into <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> addiction and lived their entire lives as prostitutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="During_the_Second_World_War">During the Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: During the Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany_during_World_War_II">Germany during World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Germany during World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_military_brothels_in_World_War_II" title="German military brothels in World War II">German military brothels in World War II</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_camp_brothels_in_World_War_II" title="German camp brothels in World War II">German camp brothels in World War II</a></div>
<p>During World War II, Germany established brothels in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagerbordell" title="Lagerbordell">Lagerbordell</a>). The women forced to work in these brothels came from the <a href="/wiki/Ravensbr%C3%BCck_concentration_camp" title="Ravensbrück concentration camp">Ravensbrück concentration camp</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Soldier's brothels (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wehrmachtsbordell" title="Wehrmachtsbordell">Wehrmachtsbordell</a>) were usually organized in already established brothels or in hotels confiscated by the Germans. The leaders of the Wehrmacht became interested in running their own brothels when sexual disease spread among the soldiers. In the controlled brothels, the women were checked frequently to avoid and treat sexually transmittable diseases (STD).</p>
<p>It is estimated that a minimum of 34,140 women from occupied states were forced to work as prostitutes during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herbermann_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herbermann-122">[122]</a></sup> In occupied Europe, the local women were often forced into prostitution. On 3 May 1941 the Foreign Ministry of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">Polish government-in-exile</a> issued a document describing the mass Nazi raids made in Polish cities with the goal of capturing young women, who later were forced to work in brothels used by German soldiers and officers. Women often tried to escape from such facilities, with at least one mass escape known to have been attempted by women in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan_during_World_War_II">Japan during World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sexual_slavery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Japan during World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="757" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg/220px-Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg/330px-Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg/440px-Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinese_girl_from_one_of_the_Japanese_Army%27s_%27comfort_battalions%27.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangoon" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>. 8 August 1945. A young <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_diaspora" title="Chinese diaspora">ethnic Chinese</a> woman who was in one of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a>'s "comfort battalions" is interviewed by an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Air_force" title="Royal Air force">RAF</a> officer.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manilajf0388_32.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Manilajf0388_32.JPG/220px-Manilajf0388_32.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Manilajf0388_32.JPG/330px-Manilajf0388_32.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Manilajf0388_32.JPG/440px-Manilajf0388_32.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manilajf0388_32.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historical Marker, in the memory of <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">Comfort women</a>; Plaza Lawton, Liwasang Bonifacio, Manila</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">Comfort women</a></div>
<p>"Comfort women" are a widely publicised example of sexual slavery. The term refers to the women, from occupied countries, who were forced to serve as sex slaves in the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">army's</a> camps during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Estimates vary as to how many women were involved, with numbers ranging from as low as 20,000 from some Japanese scholars to as high as 410,000 from some Chinese scholars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The numbers are still being researched and debated. The majority of women were taken from <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, China, and other occupied territories part of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Co-Prosperity_Sphere" title="Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere">Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere</a>.
